         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Electric Boats: Then and Now
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Four Seasons Electric Boats Website
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Boats -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            Electric boats are definitely not a new concept. What is believed to be the very first marine outboard motor was invented in 1880 by a French inventor, Gustave Trouve, and it was electric. In the early 1890's electric boats were first introduced in the United State with the formation of the
            <a href="http://www.electriclaunch.com/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; font-weight: bold; color: #003399;">
             Electric Launch Company (Elco)
            </a>
            in Bayonne, New Jersey. It was the Chicago Exposition in 1893 that put them on the map. Elco was requested to build fifty-five (55) 36-foot electric launches for this event. Ticket sales to transport people around the Chicago area lakes and rivers exceeded 1,000,000.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            That was over 120 years ago and at that time electric motors were the preferred form of propulsion. The electric "Picnic Launch" became the essence of a perfect lake cruise. Elco's company records reveal that Thomas Edison, John Jacob Astor, Admiral Dewey, George Westinghouse, and the Grand Duke Alexander of Russia were all owners of Elco electric launches.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            There were, of course, steam engines that were very powerful, yet heavy, a lot of work and not conducive to a pleasant cruising experience - especially when their boilers would explode. In the late 1800s, there were also gasoline engines. These engines at that time were called "Explosion Engines". The names were later changed to "Gasoline Engines" to make them sound safer, and more appealing to the consumer.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            After about 1920, gasoline and diesel engines became the primary propulsion units for boats - but they could never offer the quality of the electric cruising experience. At that time, electric boats lost their following, because the batteries could not carry enough energy to match the horsepower of the internal combustion engine - as folks became more intrigued with speed at the expense of comfort and quality of the boating experience.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            However the Navy's submarines continued to rely heavily on electric propulsion - because it is fundamentally reliable, efficient, and quiet. Later on, Navy ships and commercial vessels returned to electric propulsion systems for the same reasons - but using generators to create the electricity.Today, the Queen Mary II is powered exclusively with electric motors that generate 157,000 horsepower.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            <strong>
             So electric propulsion is not a "new concept" and is considered by far the most reliable form of propulsion. Not only is electric propulsion reliable and efficient, it offers the ultimate pleasure boating experience: relaxing, quiet, and NO smelly fumes.
            </strong>
            For these reasons combined with the advances in battery technology, electric pleasure boating has enjoyed a revival over the passed few decades.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            Several companies, including
            <a href="http://www.duffyboats.com/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; font-weight: bold; color: #003399;">
             Duffy Electric Boats,
            </a>
            considered the industry leader of this revival since 1970, have resurrected the electric launch and other more contemporary designs.
           </p>
           <p align="left" class="textmain" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 15px; color: #000099; line-height: 20px; text-align: -webkit-left;">
            Electric boating has become the boating lifestyle of choice for many thousands around the world in many different venues for the mainstream population.
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
       <br/>
       <table align="center" border="0" width="650">

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Green Inventor Talks Solar Powered Boats
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Aaron Colter
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Boats -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            <span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans; font-size: medium;">
            </span>
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            Before starting Tamarack Electric Boats, Montgomery Gisborne was interested in electric cars, but now he's focused on the water. Since 1993, Gisborne has been involved in the technical aspects of electric vehicles in Canada. Gisborne has been competing in the American version of the Tour del Sol since 1997, placing first in 2003, and he even created a similar race called the Canadian Clean Air Cruise.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            To date, Gisborne has logged over 31,000 miles of travel in electric vehicles. But he's not only concerned with cars. In 2003 he built one of the world's first electric snowmobiles, and two years later he founded Tamarack Electric Boats. We've covered solar boats many times, and the company's latest invention, the Loon, caught our eye and when given the opportunity, we thought readers would like to know more about a man who designs such interesting electric vehicles.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             EarthTechling (ET):
            </strong>
            You have an extensive background in electric cars, what made you want to start an electric boat company?
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             Montgomery Gisborne:
            </strong>
            Having built electric cars and electrified many other devices such as a snowmobile, I was always looking for a business opportunity in the mix. I had thought of building electric cars for a living, especially after coming in first in the 2003 American Tour del Sol electric car rally, but the reality that you cannot become GM overnight settled in. After much deliberation, I decided that the idea of a solar-powered boat must be a good one, perhaps my best, so I decided to build me first solar boat as a "science project" in 2005. The boat worked so well that I little choice but to purse it!
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             ET:
            </strong>
            Was there any specific reason that you were looking to move the company from Canada to the United States?
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             Gisborne:
            </strong>
            Sure, more people, water and sun. I think that we brought our ideas to NYS at a time when Canada seemed to focus its attention the Athabasca Tar Sands, and NYS was looking for sustainable product projects to create sustainable jobs. Then there's this crazy little piece of legislation which was brought into the North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA) called the Jones Act which prohibits Canadian companies from selling boats into the US, so we had a triumvirate of good reasons to move across the border.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             ET:
            </strong>
            Was the NYSERDA incentive program the biggest draw to relocate to Rome, NY?
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             Gisborne:
            </strong>
            No, probably not. You may have heard the old expression that "it takes a village . . . " I believe it is very true. When I passed through Rome on my solar trek across the state in 2007, i was overwhelmed by the reaction and enthusiasm of the people, more so that anywhere else I had traveled in my solar boats (which says a lot). The entire town seemed to make time to be there to catch our lines as we tossed them to shore, which really impressed me. The mayor of the town clearly saw the vision and has done more than we could ever have expected to convince us that Rome is our home. Incidentally, the first shovelful of earth removed in the construction of the Erie Canal was taken out of the ground pretty much in font of our shop on July 4th, 1817.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            I think we would have made the move anyway, without NYSERDA funding, but the funding made it possible and got us started much quicker than if we had to go it completely alone. The funding is great, but it takes more than money to create an industry, it takes drive and determination beyond my own.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             ET:
            </strong>
            Why did you decide on solar-power for the Loon above other electric options?
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <strong>
             Gisborne:
            </strong>
            There are so many reasons that make solar a natural on an electric boat. People look at my boats and say, "Oh, I get it, when the is moored at the it is picked up a free charge." While this is certainly true, the rationale for the solar goes far beyond that. For example, it dramatically reduced Peukert Effect on lead-acid batteries. Without getting into a long-winded technical discussion, this effect has a negative effect on batteries when the boat is under power, reducing the instantaneous capacity of the energy storage cells, and the solar input helps to reduce that effect, thus increasing the effective range the boat can travel on a given charge. This also helps the lead-acid batteries to better compete against other chemistries, such as nickel and lithium-based batteries at lower expense.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            I hate oil is the reason why I eschew any internal-combustion options. It is the greatest detriment to the North American economy and a threat to world peace.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; padding: 0px;">
            <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/2011/03/16/idUS427823773020110316" title="Outboard electric motor news">
             Read Entire Article
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            This is not a Loud Boat
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Ed Killer
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Boats -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            <span class="dateline">
             STUART
            </span>
            — STUART — When St. Petersburg boaters Nancy Frainetti and Jeff Springfield pulled up to the fuel dock at Hutchinson Island Marriott Marina in Stuart Tuesday afternoon, one thing was noticeably absent — engine noise.
           </p>
           <p>
            <img alt="electric boat motor | outboard electric motor | electric motor for boats | outboard electric motors" height="305" src="http://www.ddmotorsystems.com/upload/P5280056d_green_.jpg" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="electric boat motor | outboard electric motor | electric motor for boats | outboard electric motors" width="538"/>
           </p>
           <p>
            A leisurely cruise from the River Forest Yachting Center on the St. Lucie Canal in Tropical Acres to the Marriott served as the final leg of the 8-day, 250-mile “Cruise to the Atlantic.”
           </p>
           <p>
            Frainetti and Springfield, owners of Endeavour Green, builders of electric hybrid yachts, left St. Petersburg June 16 and traversed the Okeechobee Waterway in their 24-foot boat while using only $16 in electricity and a few gallons of diesel fuel.
           </p>
           <p>
            “We did this to show people that this is not a ‘toy boat,’” said Springfield, a longtime captain who said many boaters think electric-powered boats are typically for small lakes and short trips. “A typical boating family might enjoy a 20-mile trip. We had legs of this trip of 40, 47 and on Monday, 52 miles in a day.”
           </p>
           <p>
            The technology behind the Endeavour involves a 48 volt array of batteries that turn the 13 horsepower D &amp; D motor. The electric motor uses a twin belt setup to turn the drive shaft for a 3-blade bronze inboard propeller.
           </p>
           <p>
            The batteries can be charged at home or marina by plugging into a 110 volt outlet. To recharge the batteries while under way, a 3.5 kilowatt Master Volt Whisper diesel generator is employed. During the 8-day trip, Springfield said only nine hours were put on the generator and at 3.8 hours per gallon, they needed less than three gallons of diesel.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Endeavour provided comfortable passage, Frainetti said, despite record heat during their trip. A full-length canvas top — one that can fold down and serve as a boat cover when not in use — shades a large area.
           </p>
           <p>
            “We endured a little weather — but that’s something boaters are used to handling,” Frainetti said. “It got a little hot out on Lake Okeechobee Monday, but we managed to keep it from baking our brains.”
           </p>
           <p>
            Frainetti said that although the Endeavour has Eisenglass and air conditioning, they survived without it.
           </p>
           <p>
            Frainetti said she saw several manatees during the trip and counted 38 alligators while crossing Lake Okeechobee.
           </p>
           <p>
            Springfield said the hybrid technology is receiving a lot of interest from the boating community. He said that one selling feature is the simplicity of its design.
           </p>
           <p>
            “It’s an easy boat to own,” Springfield said. “It’s very simple — there are no complex systems. All the electrical components are solid state design. There are no fumes, vibration or noise. And because you are carrying little or no fuel, insurance rates are great.”
           </p>
           <p>
            For more information visit
            <a href="http://www.EndeavourGreen.com">
             www.EndeavourGreen.com
            </a>
            or call (727) 573-5377.
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Hybrid boats making waves in South Florida
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Allison Bybee
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Boats -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
           </p>
           <p style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1em; padding: 0px; margin: 0px 0px 1em 0px;">
            A brand new boat making waves in South Florida, and it runs on batteries. The Endeavour Green Company, part of the Endeavour Catamaran Corporation, showed off it's "green" boat. Co-owners, Nancy Frainetti and Jeff Stringfield, traveled from Saint Petersburg to Stuart. They did it all on battery power, no gas or diesel fuel needed, unless you want to use the back-up generator on board. The Endeavor Green Company created the boat, which is equivalent to a gas or diesel fueled deck boat. The starting cost is around $42,000. The owners say it's well worth the price, and it helps the environment. Endeavour Co-owner, Nancy Frainetti, says, "We have no emissions on the electric propulsion. So, it's as green as can be. What a wonderful benefit."
           </p>
           <p>
            <img alt="electric boat motor | outboard electric motors" height="386" src="http://www.ddmotorsystems.com/upload/EndeavourHybrid.jpg" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="electric boat motor | outboard electric motors" width="515"/>
           </p>
           <p style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1em; padding: 0px; margin: 0px 0px 1em 0px;">
            The boat is also decked out with a bathroom on board and air conditioning. It charges up each night, and usually costs only $1.50. Take that versus a gas or diesel engine that could cost you anywhere from $50 to $75 dollars a day to gas up.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            How to Build an Electric Motorcycle
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Stryker at Instructables.com
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Motorcycles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <h2>
            <strong>
             Step One
            </strong>
           </h2>
           <p>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I only work 3 miles from home but with gas prices getting out of control, I thought it would be great to have an
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px; text-decoration: underline;">
                electric motorcycle
               </span>
              </strong>
             </span>
             . I've always wanted an
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             and decided that doing an
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle conversion
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             with an
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle motor
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             would be a good EV project, keeping costs down, and be fun to ride.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             This project took about 3 months of research and development (not counting waiting for parts to come in or help from a friend with the welding). All in all, it cost about $3000 to build an
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
              <strong>
               <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
                electric motorcycle
               </span>
              </strong>
             </span>
             with a high performance
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle motor
              </strong>
             </span>
             . This may take a long time to pay off in gas savings, but if you add the fun of building and all of the environmental benefits, it was well worth the effort. With a top
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle motor
              </strong>
             </span>
             speed of over 70 mph and 10 miles per charge, this
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle
              </strong>
             </span>
             is perfect for me. The following instructable will not give you exact step by step instructions, but if you have some mechanical skills and welding ability you should be okay. A little knowledge of
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle motor
              </strong>
             </span>
             maintenance wouldn't hurt, too. However, I just read the user's manual and learned as I went.
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <h2>
            Step 2
           </h2>
           <p>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Every motorbike is different but the basic components can be the same. Below is a list of the parts I used and where I got them, but you will have to do some research to figure out what fits your bike and requirements. Check out the
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle
              </strong>
             </span>
             photos at the bottom to see what I bought and the
            </span>
            <a href="http://www.austinev.org/evalbum/type/MTCY" rel="nofollow" style="color: #ff5200; text-decoration: none; cursor: pointer; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             EVAlbum
            </a>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             for other
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle conversions
              </strong>
             </span>
             .
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Frame
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : I looked at many different bike styles and decided on a 1984 Honda Interceptor for my
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle conversion
              </strong>
             </span>
             for a few reasons:
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             1) I like the style of bike, not a total crotch rocket but not a hog either, with room for
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle
              </strong>
             </span>
             batteries inside the frame.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             2) The seller on Ebay was close to my house. And the bike didn't run, so it only cost $600 which is a perfect price for your first time
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle conversion
              </strong>
             </span>
             . If you have an old bike or someone will donate one then that's great--but for the rest of us, try the local paper, junk yards, Craig's List or ebay motors.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px; text-decoration: underline;">
              Electric Motorcycle Motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             :
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             After reading other
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle conversion
              </strong>
             </span>
             specs (and knowing that I wanted to go faster than a moped), I chose a 72V
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle motor
              </strong>
             </span>
             (D&amp;D Motorsystems carries many options), because it's weight and dimensions where good for my frame.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <strong>
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
               Electric Motorcycle
              </span>
             </strong>
             Batteries
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : I went with 6 Yellow Top Optima batteries from
            </span>
            <a href="http://www.remybattery.com/" rel="nofollow" style="color: #ff5200; text-decoration: none; cursor: pointer; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             remybattery.com
            </a>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             because they are sealed and have received great reviews. After making cardboard mock ups of the D23 model I realized that there was no way six full sized batteries would fit and still look good. I ended up getting the D51 model. Half the size and weight but also half the storage.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px; text-decoration: underline;">
              Electric Motorcycle Controller
             </strong>
            </span>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : You have to match your
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               electric motorcycle controller
              </span>
             </strong>
             to your voltage but the amperage is up to your budget. More amps = more power and more cost. It seems that there are only two real choices: Alltrax or Curtis. You'll have to decide for yourself, but I went with the 72V 450Amp Alltrax.(D&amp;D Motor Systems carries these) Don't waste your time trying to build a potimeter on an old throttle--just buy a pre-made one and be done with it. I got the Magura 0-5K Twist grip throttle.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              Electric Motorcycle
             </span>
             Charger
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : You have to match your charger with your voltage but the speed of charge in Amps is also up to your budget. I went with a Zivan NG1 but
            </span>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I have recently switched to six individual 3amp Soneil chargers to help balance the batteries.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              Electric Motorcycle
             </span>
             DC/DC Converter
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : It's safest to run with a DC/DC converter and an extra 12V battery backup but motorcycles have limited space so I am only using the converter. I purchased a Sevcon 72V Input 13.5V output from
            </span>
            <a href="http://www.evparts.com/" rel="nofollow" style="color: #ff5200; text-decoration: none; cursor: pointer; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             evparts
            </a>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             and it has working perfectly.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              Electric Motorcycle
             </span>
             Fuses
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : You'll want to get a fuse that matches your setup. I bought model ANN 400 w/ holder.(D&amp;D Motor Systems carries these)
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <strong>
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
               Electric Motorcycle
              </span>
             </strong>
             Solenoid
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             : This is a device that you hook up to your existing key ignition on 12Volts and it will close the loop so you get the full power to your controller. An excellent Solenoid is the
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               Albright SW-180B-12
              </span>
             </strong>
             .(D&amp;D Motor Systems carries these)
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <strong>
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
               Electric Motorcycle
              </span>
             </strong>
             Battery cable and connectors
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             - I bought about 10 feet of 2 GA wire from WAL-MART and cut it to length. Using Lugs,
            </span>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I soldered and used heat shrink tubing on each end. I highly recommend battery terminal covers for safety.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <strong>
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
               Electric Motorcycle
              </span>
             </strong>
             Instruments
            </strong>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I chose an E-meter(Link 10) w/ Prescaler add on for 72V use instead of a bunch of different meters. As an added feature I wired up the ignition switch to the neutral indicator to show me when the bike was on.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             <strong>
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
               Electric Motorcycle
              </span>
             </strong>
             Other parts
            </strong>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Wire - 12GA different colors and heat shrink tubing (large and small sizes)
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Electrical tape
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Wire connectors
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Wire wrap
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <strong style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Tools
            </strong>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Basic shop tools are required such as a socket set, screw drivers,wire stripper, etc. Additionally a volt meter, metal grinder and crimper are used in this
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle conversion
              </strong>
             </span>
             project.
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <h2>
            Step 3
           </h2>
           <p>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Start the
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle conversion
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             by removing all of those nasty internal combustion engine parts. Remove the gas tank and using your grinder or other cutting tool to cut out the bottom. This makes room for extra batteries or components. (
            </span>
            <em style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Make sure all gas is out before cutting
            </em>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             ) Reference your owners manual often during any
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px; text-decoration: underline;">
                electric motorcycle conversions
               </span>
              </strong>
             </span>
             so that you don't cut any necessary wires, and try to sell some of the parts to help pay for this
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle conversion
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             project.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Next, make cardboard mock ups of all of your batteries and electronic components to see how and where things are going to fit. Take a look at my
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px; text-decoration: underline;">
                electric motorcycle conversions
               </span>
              </strong>
             </span>
             pictures to see how I fit everything, believe me that taking the time to make accurate cardboard mock ups is well worth the effort.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Now for the hard part. You need a secure battery box and
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle motor
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             mount for any
             <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
              <strong>
               <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
                electric motorcycle
               </span>
               <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
                conversion
               </span>
              </strong>
             </span>
             . I had a friend weld it up for me and he did a fantastic job. From the photos you can see that he first strung up the
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
               <strong>
                electric motorcycle motor
               </strong>
              </span>
             </span>
             to allow for minor adjustment to be made before cutting the
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px; text-decoration: underline;">
                electric motorcycle motor
               </span>
              </strong>
             </span>
             mount plate. After that was cut he made a nice chain and sprocket enclosure with a door and welded them onto the frame.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Next he fabricated the battery rack and gave each battery a swing arm closure to give a tight fit yet still allow me to get them out easily. Half inch foam padding spacers are between each battery to help cushion the stack--but believe me, they aren't going anywhere. The last thing
            </span>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             he did was weld in metal plates for mounting my
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle motor
              </strong>
             </span>
             .
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             After you get your
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle motor
              </strong>
             </span>
             mount and battery compartment all welded up, take some time to clean up the frame of your bike. I removed any rust spots and chipped paint that I could find. Then I used some metallic gray and black spray paint. This makes a world of difference and costs very little.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I made a fake gas cap and ran the power cord from the charger up the frame and out the top.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Now that you have all of the welding done and your
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle
              </strong>
             </span>
             frame looks great, let's install the electrical components and start wiring it up your electric motorcycle conversion.
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <h2>
            Step 4
           </h2>
           <p>
            <span data-mce-mark="1" style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Wiring. This depends on the
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle
              </strong>
             </span>
             components you buy. See the manufacturers wiring diagrams.
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <h2>
            Step 5
           </h2>
           <p>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Double check all of your connections and tighten every bolt.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I wanted my
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric motorcycle conversions
              </strong>
             </span>
             bike to look as good as it rides, so I had all of the panels painted and custom graphics made up by
            </span>
            <a href="http://www.worldsendimages.com/" rel="nofollow" style="color: #ff5200; text-decoration: none; cursor: pointer; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             worldsendimages
            </a>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             .
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Using a serial cable and laptop, tweak the
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               electric motorcycle controller
              </span>
             </strong>
             program for your riding preferences.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             Lastly, I got the
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               electric motorcycle conversion
              </span>
             </strong>
             bike inspected and insured. (Be prepared for the dealership mechanics to swarm and hit you with a bunch of questions and jokes about failing the emissions test).
            </span>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <br style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;"/>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             I know these weren't step by step building instructions, but that's because of the complexity of this electric motorcycle conversion project and variables in component use. My intention was to give you the motivation to build your own by seeing how I did it and make it easier by supplying the
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               electric motorcycle parts
              </span>
             </strong>
             list and a wiring diagram.
            </span>
            <span style="color: #333333; font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 18px;">
             MSD
            </span>
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            2012 Brutus Electric Motorcycle Promises To Be Green, Mean
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Nikki Gordon-Bloomfield
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Motorcycles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Think about the names given to electric cars and
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycles
             </strong>
            </span>
            on the market today.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Most, if not all, are a play on the concept of all-electric, zero tailpipe emissions travel.
            <img alt="Brutus Motorcycle" height="418" src="http://www.blogcdn.com/green.autoblog.com/media/2011/10/brutus-original-628.jpg" width="628"/>
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            So when we heard about a team of engineers in Henderson, Nevada who were developing a new
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              electric motorcycle
             </span>
            </strong>
            called
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2,
            </em>
            we had to investigate.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            <strong style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Retro Styled, Classic Charm
            </strong>
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Squint at the all-electric
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2
            </em>
            and you’d be forgiven for thinking it was a classic Harley Davidson bobber or perhaps an Orange County Chopper. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              build electric motorcycle
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Either that, or a working prop from a film set in a post-appocolyptic future, Mel Gibson optional.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Designed from the ground up to be the living embodiment of a sports cruiser,
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2
            </em>
            is the first
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycle
             </strong>
            </span>
            we’ve seen that caters directly to fans of classic American motorcycles.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2
            </em>
            is also the first real stealth
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycle motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            we’ve seen. Unless you look at it closely, it doesn't immediately appear electric.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            In fact, park it up beside similar gas motorcycles, and we think you’d have a tough time telling it apart from the rest.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            <strong style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             It Isn’t Just Tough By Name
            </strong>
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            But as many classic motorcycle fans will tell you, good looks and a tough name will only get a motorcycle so far.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            In order to be considered a real motorcycle, it has to perform like one.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            That’s no problem for
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2
            </em>
            , claims Chris Bell, the original designer and owner of Brutus Electric Motorcycles.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Although it hasn’t had any official range, or
            <a class="itxtrst itxtrsta itxthook" href="http://www.greencarreports.com/news/1072106_2012-brutus-electric-motorcycle-promises-to-be-green-mean" id="itxthook1" rel="nofollow" style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #006400; float: none !important; left: auto; right: auto; top: auto; bottom: auto; border-top-style: none; border-right-style: none; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: none; border-width: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: normal; text-align: left; position: static !important; display: inline !important; font-family: inherit; padding-top: 0px; padding-right: 0px; padding-bottom: 1px; padding-left: 0px; border-bottom-color: #006400; border-bottom-width: 0.1em; margin: 0px !important;">
             <span class="itxtrst itxtrstspan itxthookspan" id="itxthook1w0" style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; float: none; left: auto; right: auto; top: auto; bottom: auto; border-top-style: none; border-right-style: none; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: none; border-width: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; background-color: transparent; position: static; display: inline; font-family: inherit; font-size: inherit; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; border-bottom-width: 2px; border-bottom-color: transparent; padding: 0px !important; margin: 0px !important;">
              performance
             </span>
            </a>
            tests, Bell claims the 535-pound motorcycle can spring from 0-60 mph in around 4.7 seconds, reach a top speed of over 100 mph, and travel over 100 miles per charge.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            These impressive performance figures are apparently down to a five-speed clutchless transmission, a
            <a class="itxtrst itxtrsta itxthook" href="http://www.greencarreports.com/news/1072106_2012-brutus-electric-motorcycle-promises-to-be-green-mean" id="itxthook2" rel="nofollow" style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #006400; float: none !important; left: auto; right: auto; top: auto; bottom: auto; border-top-style: none; border-right-style: none; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: none; border-width: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: normal; text-align: left; position: static !important; display: inline !important; font-family: inherit; padding-top: 0px; padding-right: 0px; padding-bottom: 1px; padding-left: 0px; border-bottom-color: #006400; border-bottom-width: 0.1em; margin: 0px !important;">
             <span class="itxtrst itxtrstspan itxthookspan" id="itxthook2w0" style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; float: none; left: auto; right: auto; top: auto; bottom: auto; border-top-style: none; border-right-style: none; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: none; border-width: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; background-color: transparent; position: static; display: inline; font-family: inherit; font-size: inherit; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; border-bottom-width: 2px; border-bottom-color: transparent; padding: 0px !important; margin: 0px !important;">
              powerful
             </span>
            </a>
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              D&amp;D Motor Systems
             </strong>
            </span>
            DC motor, and a liquid-cooled Zilla controller more commonly found in electric drag race cars like
            <a href="http://www.greencarreports.com/news/1061309_exclusive-black-current-iii-electric-drag-champion--whats-really-under-the-hood" style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #0070bb; text-decoration: none;">
             BlackCurrent III
            </a>
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            There aren’t any details published on battery pack capacity, although Bell claims
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2
            </em>
            should recharge its 144-volt lithium-ion battery pack in 3 hours from an available 110-volt wall outlet. Using some basic math, we think that translates to a battery capacity of between 4 and 5 kilowatt-hours. (
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              build electric motorcycle
             </span>
             )
            </strong>
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            <strong style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Forbidden Fruit?
            </strong>
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            Here’s the catch: while
            <em style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial;">
             Brutus 2
            </em>
            is certainly an real
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycle motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            built for real motorcyclists, it hasn’t entered production yet.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            According to Bell, that should happen some time this year, provided current deals being discussed with various parts and manufacturing companies are signed.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            But right now, the all-electric beast is nothing more than an impressive prototype motorcycle awaiting production.
           </p>
           <p style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; font-family: Candara, 'Lucida Sans', 'Lucida Grande', Verdana; font-size: 14px;">
            And that’s a real shame, because we think this is exactly the kind of electric motorcycle that needs to be built in order to help convince mainstream motorcyclists that electric powered motorcycles can be mean and
            <a class="nwslinks_visible" href="http://www.greencarreports.com/category/green,new" style="outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #0070bb; text-decoration: none;">
             green
            </a>
            at the same time. (
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              build electric motorcycle
             </span>
             )  MSD
            </strong>
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
