        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            E-motorcycle offers hot ride, keeps the cool
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Angeli Duffin
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Motorcycles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p style="margin-top: 10px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            Making the case for an electric car - higher up-front costs, but then much less expensive and
            <a class="kLink" href="http://www.tgdaily.com/sustainability-features/60963-e-motorcycle-offers-hot-ride-keeps-the-cool" id="KonaLink0" style="border-style: none !important; border-color: transparent !important; border-image: initial !important; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #346200; -webkit-transition-property: color; -webkit-transition-duration: 0.25s; -webkit-transition-timing-function: ease; -webkit-transition-delay: initial; cursor: pointer; background-image: none !important; background-attachment: initial !important; background-origin: initial !important; background-clip: initial !important; background-color: transparent !important; display: inline !important; top: 0px; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; left: 0px; position: static; border-width: 0px !important; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">
             <span style="font-family: inherit !important; font-size: inherit !important; position: static; color: #346200;">
              <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: #346200; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
               environmentally
              </span>
             </span>
            </a>
            damaging to operate - to someone switching from a gasoline-powered car is pretty straightforward.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            But convincing someone to trade in their Harley for an
            <a href="../ElectricMotorcycles.php">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycle
             </strong>
            </a>
            ? That could be more challenging. There has to be an element of cool. And speed.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            <img alt="electric motorcycle conversion | electric motorcycle conversions" height="366" src="../Electric_Motorcycle.jpg" style="border-style: initial; border-color: initial; margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 20px; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; font-style: inherit; font-family: inherit; vertical-align: baseline; float: left; border-width: 1px; padding: 5px;" title="electric motorcycle conversion | electric motorcycle conversions" width="333"/>
            Which is what two Purdue University students and AllCell Technologies set out to produce – and appear to have delivered, with an
            <span style="font-family: inherit !important; font-size: inherit !important; position: static; color: #346200;">
             <a class="kLink" href="../ElectricMotorcycles.php" id="KonaLink1" style="border-style: none !important; border-color: transparent !important; border-image: initial !important; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #346200; -webkit-transition-property: color; -webkit-transition-duration: 0.25s; -webkit-transition-timing-function: ease; -webkit-transition-delay: initial; cursor: pointer; background-image: none !important; background-attachment: initial !important; background-origin: initial !important; background-clip: initial !important; background-color: transparent !important; display: inline !important; top: 0px; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; left: 0px; position: static; border-width: 0px !important; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">
              <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: #346200; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
               electric
              </span>
              <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: #346200; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
               motorcycle
              </span>
             </a>
            </span>
            that packs 72 kilowatts of power and, according to early tests, can hit 120 mph and cover 120 miles on a charge, according to AllCell.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            The company said the trick to creating this high-performance bike was in the 10.6 kilowatt-hour
            <a class="kLink" href="http://www.tgdaily.com/sustainability-features/60963-e-motorcycle-offers-hot-ride-keeps-the-cool" id="KonaLink2" style="border-style: none !important; border-color: transparent !important; border-image: initial !important; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #346200; -webkit-transition-property: color; -webkit-transition-duration: 0.25s; -webkit-transition-timing-function: ease; -webkit-transition-delay: initial; cursor: pointer; background-image: none !important; background-attachment: initial !important; background-origin: initial !important; background-clip: initial !important; background-color: transparent !important; display: inline !important; top: 0px; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; left: 0px; position: static; border-width: 0px !important; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">
             <span style="font-family: inherit !important; font-size: inherit !important; position: static; color: #346200;">
              <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: initial; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
               lithium
              </span>
              <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: initial; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
               ion
              </span>
             </span>
            </a>
            battery that uses AllCell’s thermal management material.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            The phase change material graphite composite (PCM-graphite) controls the impact if one cell has an internal short circuit, and the PCM material absorbs and distributes heat away from the
            <a class="kLink" href="http://www.tgdaily.com/sustainability-features/60963-e-motorcycle-offers-hot-ride-keeps-the-cool" id="KonaLink3" style="border-style: none !important; border-color: transparent !important; border-image: initial !important; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; outline-style: none; outline-width: initial; outline-color: initial; color: #346200; -webkit-transition-property: color; -webkit-transition-duration: 0.25s; -webkit-transition-timing-function: ease; -webkit-transition-delay: initial; cursor: pointer; background-image: none !important; background-attachment: initial !important; background-origin: initial !important; background-clip: initial !important; background-color: transparent !important; display: inline !important; top: 0px; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; left: 0px; position: static; border-width: 0px !important; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;">
             <span style="font-family: inherit !important; font-size: inherit !important; position: static; color: #346200;">
              <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: initial; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
               battery
              </span>
             </span>
            </a>
            , protecting the cells and maximizing battery life.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            While some motorcyclists might enjoy being daredevils, with this motorcycle riders can let ‘er rip and concentrate on driving without worrying about unnecessary things like an overheating battery. Apart from the battery,
            <strong>
             electric vehicle
            </strong>
            experts Tesla
            <span class="kLink" style="padding-top: 0px !important; padding-right: 0px !important; padding-bottom: 1px !important; padding-left: 0px !important; border-top-width: 0px !important; border-right-width: 0px !important; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 0px !important; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-style: inherit; font-size: inherit !important; font-family: inherit !important; vertical-align: baseline; border-top-style: none !important; border-top-color: initial !important; border-left-style: none !important; border-left-color: initial !important; border-right-style: none !important; border-right-color: initial !important; border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-color: initial; background-image: none; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; width: auto !important; float: none !important; display: inline !important; position: static; margin: 0px;">
             Motors
            </span>
            and Delphi Corporation also provided support for the project, AllCell said.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            This team is not alone in the quest for the superior
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycle motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            . There seems to be quite a trend in
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <a href="../ElectricMotorcycles.php">
               m
              </a>
              otorcycle conversion to electric
             </span>
            </strong>
            in garages, notably from a fellow Purdue student who we reported used solar power to power his, yes that’s right, Solar Cycle.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-bottom: 10px; margin-left: 0px; border-style: initial; border-color: initial; border-image: initial; font-size: 13px; font-family: Georgia, Times, serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: #333333; line-height: 19px; text-align: -webkit-auto; border-width: 0px; padding: 0px;">
            However, for those of us who aren’t that confident in our mechanical skills, there are a growing number of companies producing
            <strong>
             electric motorcycles
            </strong>
            with both coolness (largely because of their green-factor) and impressive power and speed. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motorcycle conversion
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>

         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Will Electric Motorcycles Catch On Faster Than Electric Cars?
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: By Jonathan Welsh
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Motorcycles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            The International Motorcycle Show starts in New York today, so the Jacob Javits Center will be awash in chrome-crusted cruisers weighing more than 600 pounds and packing car-size engines, and screaming superbikes with enough horsepower to fly a four-passenger airplane.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            <img alt="electric motorcycle conversion kits | electric motorcycle conversion" height="239" src="http://s.wsj.net/public/resources/images/OB-RL626_zero_E_20120119230056.jpg" title="electric motorcycle conversion kits | electric motorcycle conversion" width="359"/>
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            But some of the most intriguing machines at the show are small, light and nearly silent.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            Electric motorcycles powered by lithium batteries are beginning to look like contenders in a bike market that is increasingly concerned about fuel efficiency, emissions and noise.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            Electrics may attract customers who like the idea of two-wheel transport but are put off by the mechanical complexity of traditional motorcycles and the perceived difficulty in riding them. They may also have particular appeal to urban riders and commuters who can operate more easily within the bikes’ limited range.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            I test-rode an electric sport motorcycle called the Zero S this and week and was surprised by how appealing it is even for someone who loves the chugging rhythm of a Ducati twin or the wail of an old Honda V4. The quiet whir of the electric motor and its impressive off-the-line acceleration made the Zero ideal for city riding, where hearing nearby traffic can be as important as seeing it.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            While the motor puts out about 28 horsepower, it feels like much more, especially when accelerating from a standstill. I was able to leave menacing taxis far behind and the bike’s weight of less than 300 pounds gave it a light, athletic feel that made getting through midtown New York’s congestion enjoyable.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            The Zero S has evolved since 2009, when I rode an early version. The new bike is faster, smoother and better-looking than its predecessor and has a tighter, well-finished feel. It’s ready for prime time.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            As with electric cars, though, high prices could keep some customers away. The S and its on-road-off-road stable mate the DS start at $11,495. The higher-capacity battery that boosts range to 114 miles from about 76 miles with the standard battery also increases the price to $13,995. That amount would buy a Honda CBR1000RR, which is close to being a street-legal racing bike.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            Of course riders interested in electric motorcycles are not cross-shopping superbikes. But the Zero’s price premium could hurt sales.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            Still, the simple joy of riding the Zero could be as big a selling point as its potential fuel savings. In many ways its design and the way it rides are throwbacks to the minimalism and excitement of earlier motorcycles that drew so many people into riding decades ago.
           </p>
           <p style="margin-top: 0px; margin-right: 8px; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 8px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; line-height: 1.5em; text-align: left; padding: 0px;">
            While I tell people that my next new car will probably be electric, a battery-powered motorcycle, in some ways, would be a better fit.
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
       <br/>

           <strong>
            A new day.. a new bike. Electric Motorsports of California
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By:  azhar
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">

        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p class="MsoNormal">
            <span style="font-family: 
 
 Helvetica;">
             Oakland California USA,
             <span>
             </span>
             Electric Motorsport 
 
 Inc. has unveiled its two entries for the June/12th Isle of Man TTXGP.  In 
 
 the open class is a modified production electric motorcycle called the GPR-S. 
 
  The Electric Motorsport GPR-S were the first Production 
 
 Electricmotorcycles capable of attaining legal freeway speeds in the 
 
 USA.
            </span>
           </p>
           <p class="MsoNormal">
            <span style="font-family: 
 
 Helvetica;">
             In the Pro Class, the entry is the Electric Motorsport R144. 
 
  This conversion is based on an R1 race chassis. This motorcycle utilizes 
 
 a high performance electric motor designed and manufactured by
             <a href="http://www.ddmotorsystems.com" target="_blank" title="D&amp;D Motor Systems - High Performance Electric Motors">
              D&amp;D Motor 
 
 Systems, Inc
             </a>
             .
            </span>
           </p>
           <p class="MsoNormal">
            <img alt="motorcycle conversion to electric | electric motorcycle conversion" height="299" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_XBvzkkAd7kA/Sf6BfhxSkSI/AAAAAAAAAXc/4rGdobh_XFs/s320/IMG_3700_web.jpg" title="motorcycle conversion to electric | electric motorcycle conversion" width="448"/>
           </p>
           <p class="MsoNormal">
            <span style="font-family: 
 
 Helvetica;">
             Electric Motorsport is a technology company that specializes in 
 
 Light Electric Vehicles and electric propulsion systems.
             <span>
             </span>
             Electric Motorsport is proud to say they have supplied electric drive 
 
 systems and components to many of the TTXGP teams that will be 
 
 competing.
             <span>
             </span>
             Why does Electric Motorsport supply its 
 
 competitors with hi-performance electric drive components?
             <span>
             </span>
             Electric motorsport Founder and CEO Todd Kollin says "its mainly to 
 
 promote the technology and to have some one to race with, and besides we are 
 
 in the parts business.
             <span>
             </span>
             Racing is just the fun part and its not much 
 
 fun without competition."
            </span>
           </p>
           <p class="MsoNormal">
            <span style="font-family: Helvetica;">
             Electric Motorsport Inc has always placed an 
 
 emphasis on the Electric motorcycle as away of using renewable energy such as 
 
 solar, wind, hydroelectric, and geothermal to propel ourselves from one location 
 
 to the next.
             <span>
             </span>
             The company has sold 1000's of electric 
 
 motorcycle conversion kits.
             <span>
             </span>
             Electric Motorsport even sells books 
 
 on how to convert your old gas motorcycle to electric.
             <span>
             </span>
             These 
 
 conversions are great if you have a old bike that does not run so well or has a 
 
 blown engine.
             <span>
             </span>
             An electric conversion can bring the thing 
 
 back to life but without having to deal with oil, gas, noise, fumes, warm ups,tune 
 
 ups, gear boxes, clutches.

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Honda Promises An Electric Motorcycle By 2010
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Tony Borroz
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Motorcycles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            <img alt="electric motorcycle conversion | electric motorcycle conversions" height="363" src="https://www.wired.com/images_blogs/photos/uncategorized/2008/12/19/08_cbr1000rr.jpg" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="electric motorcycle conversion | electric motorcycle conversions" width="545"/>
           </p>
           <p>
            So Honda is getting into the electric motorcycle biz huh? Well, now we know what they plan to do with all the engineering talent suddenly available from their now defunct
            <a href="http://blog.wired.com/cars/2008/12/cash-strapped-
 
 a.html">
             F1
            </a>
            &amp;
            <a href="http://www.motorcyclenews.com/MCN/sport/sportresults/mcn/2008/Decem
 
 ber/15-21/dec1508-honda-quit-ama-superbikes/?R=EPI-104811">
             AMA
            </a>
            efforts.
           </p>
           <p>
            <a href="http://www.motorcyclenews.com/MCN/News/newsresults/mcn/2008/Dece
 
 mber/15-21/dec1808-2009-yamaha-r1-video/?R=EPI-105070">
             Motorcycle News
            </a>
            (via our friends at
            <a href="http://www.autobloggreen.com/2008/12/19/honda-vows-to-release-electric
 
 -motorcycle-within-2-years/">
             AutoBlogGreen
            </a>
            ) says Honda is serious about building a workable Ebike and selling it to the likes of you and me by 2010. Sure, that sounds plausible. Honda has the engineering grunt and it pretty much has the whole motorcycle thing down, so it seems like a lead pipe cinch.
           </p>
           <p>
            But is it?
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <div class="entry -more">
            <p>
             Not exactly. Honda faces the same hurdles everyone else does:
             <a href="http://auto.howstuffworks.com/electric-car4.htm">
              range
             </a>
             and
             <a href="http://auto.howstuffworks.com/electric-car5.htm">
              recharge times
             </a>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             I spent some time with an outfit made electric scooters and motorcycles. It was a real geeky operation making scooters and souped-up jobs custom-built to customers' needs, desires and checkbooks. Once or twice a year someone with sacks of money would come in and say something along the lines of "Take my
             <a href="http://www.gsxr.com/">
              GSX-R
             </a>
             and make it electric." We would, but we'd invariably face the same challenges everyone else building EVs faces: range and recharge times.
            </p>
            <p>
             Yeah, we could build an electric GSX-R that would out haul
             <a href="http://www.fanclubvalentinorossi.com/">
              Valentino Rossi
             </a>
             - for about seven to 10 miles. Then you'd stop. And then you'd have to plug it in for six or eight or 10 hours. The bike was cool, but not very practical. You couldn't take the thing up some canyon road on your way out of town to Palm Springs for a three day weekend. These will be the same limitations that Honda will face, but in a couple of not so noticeable ways, electric motorcycles play to Honda's strengths.
            </p>
            <p>
             For one, bikes are easy. They're small, light and easy to work on. You can fab up and try things on two or three test mules in an afternoon, and that's an order of magnitude or so harder with cars. For another, Honda is a bike company. Yeah, I know, tell that to
             <a href="http://www.senna.com.br/">
              Ayrton Senna
             </a>
             and
             <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alain_Prost%22">
              Alain Prost
             </a>
             and
             <a href="http://www.mclaren.com/">
              Ron Dennis,
             </a>
             but it started out primarily as a bike company (OK, go back far enough and it started out as a piston ring company, but still...) then morphed into a car company. What Honda learns from making an Ebike over the next two years can, hopefully, migrate to cars.
            </p>
            <p>
             Honda confirms working with bikes is favorable on a number of levels.
            </p>
            <p>
             "History shows that motorcycles remain strong in a difficult market environment and have always supported Honda in difficult times," says CEO
             <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Takeo_Fukui">
              Takeo Fukui
             </a>
             . "People showed renewed interest in the value of motorcycles which consume less fuel for commuting purposes as well as for their easy-to-own/easy-to-use efficiency."
            </p>
            <p>
             Good point, Takeo. That's another thing bikes got going for them: They're cheap.
            </p>
            <p>
             Pound for pound and dollar for dollar motorcycles are the best bet for enthusiast fun. Not for me, of course, because I am comically and frighteningly uncoordinated and that's never a good thing on a motorcycle. But you get my point.
            </p>
            <p>
             Think of what Honda is doing as a real world proof of concept scheme. Make an electric motorcycle. Make it work. Make it work better. Then import the technology into a car. Repeat the process.
            </p>
            <p>
             What could go wrong?
            </p>
            <p>
             <em>
              Photo: Honda.
             </em>
            </p>
           </div>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
       <br/>
      </div>

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            An Electric Hybrid Truck Designed For Utility Fleets
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Ucilia Wang
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Vehicles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            If you can soup up a plug-in hybrid electric vehicle(
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV
             </span>
            </strong>
            )
            <span style="background-color: transparent;">
             , what features would you want? For some fleet managers, turning plug-in hybrids into a source for powering up construction tools or buildings during a blackout is high on the list.
            </span>
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            <img alt="electric car conversion | electric car motors kits | EV parts | EV conversion | electric cars kits" height="189" src="http://blogs-images.forbes.com/uciliawang/files/2012/01/PGE-eREV-300x187.jpg" style="width: 461px; height: 291px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="EV parts | EV conversion | electric cars kits" width="295"/>
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            That’ why Pacific Gas &amp; Electric Co. has been helping VIA Motors to convert new General Motors trucks into plug-in hybrids with the ability to export a large amount of power. The utility, the largest in California, envisions sending a bunch of these trucks into the field for routine maintenance work and to deal with emergencies. The amount of exportable power here will be large enough to run hydraulic lifts to send workers up the powerlines to do repairs or serve as backup power for homes while workers fix faulty circuits or transformers, said Dave Meisel, director of transportation services at PG&amp;E. (
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV motors
             </span>
            </strong>
            )
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            Hybrid cars offer fuel savings over time – the price of gasoline has risen and will continue to increase at greater rates than the price of electricity – as well as environmental benefits such as lower emissions, he said. As federal and states introduce stricter fuel economy and emission standards, businesses must comply by buying vehicles with more fuel-efficient engines or ones that run on cleaner sources of fuels. But alternative-fuel vehicles also tend to cost more partly because they aren’t made in large volumes, and fleet managers very much focus on the payback period of their investments. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motor conversion kits
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            Adding the exportable power feature creates additional savings for fleet owners like PG&amp;E, Meisel said. It eliminates the need for buying portable generators that run on fossil fuels, for example. Using the hybrid trucks to reduce the length of a blackout also is an attractive proposition for utilities, which face fines if their customers experience a high number of outages or if they can’t restore power quickly.
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            “We are looking at broader savings that a lot of people are not looking at,” Meisel said. “When I look at the total operational savings, including fuel savings, the math starts to look really nice.” PG&amp;E has about 9,000 vehicles in its fleet, and roughly 3,100 of them run on alternative fuels, such as natural gas, electricity and biodiesel. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric car motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            PG&amp;E has been field-testing two
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              EV
             </strong>
            </span>
            trucks since last year and giving the car company feedback about its experience and suggestions for improvements. The utility estimates that the trucks could deliver annual fuel maintenance savings of $7000 per vehicle compared with conventional trucks, said Greg Pruett, senior vice president of corporate affairs at PG&amp;E, during a press event at the
            <a href="http://www.forbes.com/places/mi/detroit/" style="border-image: initial; outline-width: initial; outline-style: none; outline-color: initial; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; color: #666666; padding: 0px; margin: 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
             Detroit
            </a>
            auto show earlier this month when VIA discussed its plans to launch not just hybrid trucks but also hybrid SUVs and vans. VIA plans to convert only GM models, such as the Chevy Silverado, for now.
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            VIA has developed a powertrain that includes a 24 kilowatt-hour lithium-ion battery pack, which can last up to 40 miles per charge. The gasoline engine is for generating electricity to run the
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric car motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            , which moves the wheels. The company is putting its technology in brand new vehicles only, not used cars. When VIA Motors showed up at the Detroit auto show, its executives rattled off a list of things that people can do with vehicles that double as power generators, such as catering to outdoor parties and running outdoor concerts.
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            “Think of a 3-day camping trip where you have unlimited power with the car you drive into the woods with,” said Bob Lutz, a member of VIA’s board of directors and the former vice chairman of GM, during a press conference at the auto show.
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            The two VIA trucks PG&amp;E has been trying out cost about $400,000 total, Meisel said. The trucks are the early version of what VIA plans to produce commercially later this year, Meisel said. The price for the trucks at “low volumes” should be in the $70,000 range, and it should continue to drop as production increases, he added. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motor conversion kits
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            VIA isn’t the only company PG&amp;E is turning to for converted hybrids with exportable power. The utility also is considering vehicles from Electric Vehicle
            <a href="http://www.forbes.com/international/" style="border-image: initial; outline-width: initial; outline-style: none; outline-color: initial; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; color: #666666; padding: 0px; margin: 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
             International
            </a>
            , which turns beefier pickup trucks to plug-in hybrids. VIA’s truck delivers 15 kilowatts of exportable power and is working on boosting that to 50 kilowatts while Electric Vehicle (
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV
             </span>
            </strong>
            ) International is working on trucks with 100 kilowatts of exportable power. Figuring out a good way to cool the equipment that generates and routes the power becomes a greater hurdle as the size of exportable power increases.
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            PG&amp;E and other fleet owners are turning to companies that can do after-market conversion for now partly because major automakers have yet to introduce the plug-in hybrid version of the trucks that the fleet owners want to buy.(
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              EV motors
             </strong>
            </span>
            ) But that day will come if consumers continue to show interest in electric cars (and the prices for them drop). When that happens, companies such as VIA Motors may find it difficult to compete, said Kevin See, an analyst with Lux Research.
           </p>
           <p style="border-image: initial; outline-width: 0px; outline-style: initial; outline-color: initial; font-size: 18px; vertical-align: baseline; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: transparent; line-height: 24px; font-family: Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: left; padding: 0px; margin: 15px 0px 15px 0px; border: 0px initial initial;">
            “There may be a short-lived window for them to make their mark,” See said. “I wouldn’t expect their businesses to be long-term because of the competition that will enter the market. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              EV motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            )”  MSD
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>

        <tr>
         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Electric vehicle owners can get a charge in Media now
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Susan L. Serbin
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Vehicles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             Media Borough has created another reason to make “Everybody’s Hometown” a destination. This time an initiative will make downtown the hometown for owners of
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric vehicles
              </strong>
             </span>
             (
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               EV
              </span>
             </strong>
             ).
            </span>
           </p>
           <p>
            <img alt="EV parts | EV conversion | electric cars kits" height="373" src="http://images.townnews.com/delconewsnetwork.com/content/articles/2012/01/24/media_town_talk/news/doc4f1ee90f7b7847491467451.jpg" title="EV parts | EV conversion | electric cars kits" width="497"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             As only the third known location in Delaware County, Media has inaugurated a charging station in the municipal parking lot next to the Media Fire Department, across from Media-Upper Providence Library and one block from all that State Street has to offer.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             The borough is participating in a pilot project for
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               EV
              </span>
             </strong>
             charging powered by 100 percent Pennsylvania wind energy. Borough officials and Community Energy, Inc. had the ribbon cutting recently, with attendance by representatives of the energy firm, Mayor Bob McMahon, Councilman Eric Stein, Environmental Advisory Council Chair Walt Cressler and several other borough staff member.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             While the technology includes several cutting-edge elements, charging station operation is fairly simple: pull into the dedicated parking space (lot is between Jasper and Front streets just east of Jackson Street); plug the
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               electric vehicle
              </span>
             </strong>
             (
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               EV
              </span>
             </strong>
             ) into the charger; dine, shop or attend to other borough business. In the span of an hour or two,
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               EVs
              </strong>
             </span>
             can be charged enough for at least several dozen miles.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             “We are pleased to be partnering with Media Borough and the Media Fire Company as this becomes one of the first charging stations in the county,” said Jay Carlis, Vice President of Retail Marketing for Community Energy, Inc. based in Radnor. “This pilot project, funded by the Pennsylvania Department of Environmental Protection, comes early in the
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               electric vehicle
              </span>
             </strong>
             transition. At the government level, Media has been a leader in environmental sustainability. This is a great location for residents and visitors.”
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             Carlis said there are
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric vehicle
              </strong>
             </span>
             (
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               EV
              </span>
             </strong>
             ) charging stations in Radnor and Wayne and only a handful in the state, placing the borough in the forefront of the technology. To kick off the enterprise, he drove a Chevrolet Volt and hooked it up to demonstrate the virtual plug, charge and go technique.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             Representatives from Thomas Chevrolet brought a second Volt. Amy Ercolani of Thomas said the dealership has sold several Volts, has one in stock, and expects the manufacturer to supply a small but steady stream of the model, which has a gasoline back-up capability.
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               EVs
              </strong>
             </span>
             are available from other automotive manufacturers as well.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             Running at a 240-volt service, the public station works twice as fast as a charge from, for example, a home outlet which is generally half the volts. An hour charge is expected to cost $3.50 with Community Energy paying a fee to the borough for the actual electric used. The mileage value of a charge varies depending on the
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric vehicle
              </strong>
             </span>
             and road conditions, not unlike gas mileage. Not surprisingly, there are “apps” which can monitor the charge from mobile devices.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             In the borough’s view, the station sends multiple signals about the alternative energy commitment which already includes a solar energy grid and wind-generated electricity purchase.
            </span>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <br style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px; padding: 0px; margin: 0px;"/>
            <span style="color: #363636; font-family: Helvetica, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 19px;">
             “I’m a strong supporter of renewable energy and any
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               electric car conversion
              </strong>
             </span>
             . I have solar energy at my home, so I’m not just talking theoretically,” said Stein, liaison to the Environmental Advisory Council. “It’s good for the economy, and good for the environment.”   MSD
            </span>

         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            Utilities: Grid can handle influx of electric cars
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: AP
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Vehicles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            Which draws more juice from the electric grid, a big-screen plasma television or recharging an
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV
             </span>
            </strong>
            (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric vehicle
             </strong>
            </span>
            )?
           </p>
           <p>
            The answer is the car. But the electricity draw by plasma televisions is easing the minds of utility company executives across the nation as they plan for what is likely to be an
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric car conversion
             </strong>
            </span>
            of much of the country's vehicle fleet from gasoline to electricity in the coming years.
           </p>
           <p>
            Rechargeable cars, industry officials say, consume about four times the electricity as plasma TVs.
           </p>
           <p>
            But the industry already has dealt with increased electric demand from the millions of plasma TVs sold in recent years. Officials say that experience will help them deal with the vehicle fleet changeover to EV's. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motor conversion kits
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p>
            So as long as the changeover from internal combustion engines to
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric vehicles
             </strong>
            </span>
            is somewhat gradual, they should be able to handle it in the same way, Mark Duvall, program manager for electric transportation, power delivery and distribution for the Electric Power Research Institute, said Tuesday.
           </p>
           <p>
            "We've already added to the grid the equivalent of several years' production of
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV hybrids
             </span>
            </strong>
            ," Duvall said at a conference on
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              EV's
             </strong>
            </span>
            (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric vehicles
             </strong>
            </span>
            ) in San Jose. "The utilities, they stuck with it. They said, 'All right, that's what's happening. This is where the loads are going, and we're going to do this."'
           </p>
           <p>
            Automakers, such as
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              General Motors
             </strong>
            </span>
            and
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              To
              <span style="color: #004276; text-decoration: underline;">
               yota
              </span>
             </span>
            </strong>
            , are planning to bring
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV motors
             </span>
            </strong>
            to the market as early as 2010. But speakers at the Plug-In 2008 conference say it will take much longer for them to arrive in mass numbers, due in part to a current lack of large-battery manufacturing capacity. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric motor conversion kits
             </strong>
            </span>
            )  MSD
           </p>
           <p>
            <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2008/TECH/ptech/07/23/electriccars.grid.ap/index.html#cnnSTCText">
             Read More
            </a>
           </p>

         <td valign="top">
          <font color="#990000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="+1">
           <strong>
            A New (Good) Look for Electric Cars
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: JACK LOSH / LONDON
           </strong>
          </font>
         </td>
         <td align="right">
          <font color="#666666" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           Filed Under: Electric Vehicles -
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            Electric cars or EVs (electric vehicles) have been around for almost 170 years, but it's not just the limitations of battery power that have thwarted their more widespread use. Since Scottish businessman Robert Anderson pioneered the first electric carriage in the 1830s, most EV's have lacked one of the key markers of auto success: good looks. Just take a look at La Jamais Contente, designed by Belgian Camille Jenatzy in 1899, or Billard and Zarpe's space-age oddity, the Elektra King (1961). Even today's EV models — the REVA, or Zaps Zebra — are proof that the best adjective to describe most electric cars remains
            <em>
             quirky.
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            Now two new models show that green can be given a devastatingly cool makeover. Britain's Lightning GT and the U.S.-built Tesla Roadster both reach 60 m.p.h. in 4 seconds or less, their makers claim, with top speeds approaching 130 m.p.h. The Lightning GT - unveiled at London's International Motor Show last week and set to be available from the end of 2009 - sports an impressive, sleek and sexy design, drawing on Aston Martin's classic British look. Tesla, which launched its hot, little open-top two-seater a couple of years ago, has already sold out of the 2008 model and is eagerly taking reservations for 2009. Battery power has rarely, if ever, looked this good.
           </p>
           <p>
            <img alt="ev parts | ev conversion | electric cars kits" height="235" src="http://img.timeinc.net/time/daily/2008/0807/lightning_0725.jpg" title="ev parts | ev conversion | electric cars kits" width="360"/>
           </p>
           <p>
            <a href="http://www.time.com/time/business/article/0,8599,1827090,00.html?
 
 xid=feed-cnn-topics">
             Read More
            </a>
           </p>
          </font>
         </td>
        </tr>

           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">

            By: Curt Merrill - CNN
           </strong>

         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           <p>
            Larry Horsley loves that he doesn't buy much gas, even though he drives his '95 Chevy S-10 back and forth to work each day. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              Electric Car Conversion
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p>

            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              EV motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            (electric vehicle) truck into an electric wall outlet in his Douglasville, Georgia, garage and charges it overnight, instead of buying gasoline refined from mostly imported oil. Using
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              electric motor conversion kit
             </span>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              s
             </span>
            </strong>
            , many hobbyists are doing the same thing.
           </p>
           <p>
            "If I can keep a dollar from going overseas, I'll spend two dollars," he said. The whole
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric car motor conversion
             </strong>
            </span>
            , including the truck and high performance
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              EV motor
             </strong>
            </span>
            , cost him about $12,000, which parts dealers say is about standard for an
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric car conversion
             </strong>
            </span>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            Another Atlanta-area tinkerer, David Kennington, converted his Honda Civic del Sol from gasoline to an
            <strong>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              EV
             </span>
            </strong>
            for a different reason: "I'm a raging greenie," he said. (
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              Electric Car Conversion
             </strong>
            </span>
            )
           </p>
           <p>
            Both Horsley and Kennington are fed up. They're among a growing number of Americans who are refusing to wait for big-car manufacturers to deliver a mainstream
            <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
             <strong>
              electric car
             </strong>
            </span>
            , called EVs. Not only have they rebelled against the status quo by ripping out their gas-guzzling engines and replacing them with a zero-emission
            <strong>
             electric car motor
            </strong>
            , they say just about anyone can do an
            <strong>
             electric car conversion
            </strong>
            . As long as you get a good
            <strong>
             electric vehicle motor controller
            </strong>
            and
            <strong>
             electric auto motor
            </strong>
            , both can be purchased from D&amp;D Motor Systems, Inc, you are well on your way. MSD
           </p>

            How to: Build a Fuel-Less, Solar-Powered Vehicle
           </strong>
          </font>
          <br/>
          <font color="#333333" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="" size="-1">
           <strong>
            By: Collin 
 
 Dunn, Corvallis, OR, USA
           </strong>
          </font>

         <td colspan="2" style="padding-left:15px">
          <font color="#000000" face="Arial," helvetica="" sans-serif="">
           &lt;
           <p>
            TreeHugger has recently covered the Solar 
 
 Sailor and solar-powered
            <a href="http://www.ddmotorsystems.com/ElectricMotorcycles.php">
             electric bike
            </a>
            , but we've never seen anything quite like this. For the 
 
 serious DIYer, SolarVehicles.org 
 
 offers info, resources, advice and even blueprints for building your own solar-
 
 powered vehicle. Most of the models are somewhere between a scooter and a 
 
 golf cart, and, according to the pictures on the site, they even work! It may not be 
 
 the kind of thing you'd want to take on the highway or even a busy street, but 
 
 they seem perfect for putting around town. Once built, the three and four-
 
 wheeled vehicles go between 25 and 40 km/h (about 15 to 25 mph) depending on 
 
 the load/cargo and grade of the road. The site has all the info you'll need to build 
 
 your own, from wheels to solar cells to frames, so you can get yourself around 
 
 using the power of the sun.
